        </a>
        <a class="external text" href="http://cvc.instituto-camoes.pt/hlp/geografia/som44.html" rel="nofollow">
         <i>
          Algarvio
         </i>
        </a>
        —
        <a href="/wiki/Algarve" title="Algarve">
         Algarve
        </a>
        (there is a particular dialect in a small part of western Algarve).
       </li>
       <li>
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Loudspeaker.svg">
         <img alt="Loudspeaker.svg" data-file-height="20" data-file-width="20" height="11" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" width="11"/>
        </a>
        <a class="external text" href="http://cvc.instituto-camoes.pt/hlp/geografia/som1.html" rel="nofollow">
         <i>
          Minhoto
         </i>
        </a>
        —Districts of
        <a href="/wiki/Braga" title="Braga">

        </a>
        and Viana do Castelo (hinterland).
       </li>
       <li>
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Loudspeaker.svg">
         <img alt="Loudspeaker.svg" data-file-height="20" data-file-width="20" height="11" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" width="11"/>
        </a>
        <a class="external text" href="http://cvc.instituto-camoes.pt/hlp/geografia/som49.html" rel="nofollow">
         <i>
          Beirão
         </i>
         ;
         <i>
          Alto-Alentejano
         </i>
        </a>
        —Central Portugal (hinterland).
       </li>
       <li>
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Loudspeaker.svg">
         <img alt="Loudspeaker.svg" data-file-height="20" data-file-width="20" height="11" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" width="11"/>
        </a>
        <a class="external text" href="http://cvc.instituto-camoes.pt/hlp/geografia/som9.html" rel="nofollow">
         <i>
          Beirão
         </i>
        </a>
        — Central Portugal.
       </li>
       <li>
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Loudspeaker.svg">
         <img alt="Loudspeaker.svg" data-file-height="20" data-file-width="20" height="11" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" width="11"/>
        </a>
        <a class="external text" href="http://cvc.instituto-camoes.pt/hlp/geografia/som22.html" rel="nofollow">
         <i>
          Estremenho
         </i>
        </a>
        —Regions of
        <a href="/wiki/Coimbra" title="Coimbra">
         Coimbra
        </a>
        ,
        <a href="/wiki/Leiria" title="Leiria">
         Leiria
        </a>
        and
        <a href="/wiki/Lisbon" title="Lisbon">
         Lisbon
        </a>
        (this is a disputed denomination, as Coimbra is not part of "Estremadura", and the Lisbon dialect has some peculiar features that not only are not shared with the one of Coimbra, but also are significantly distinct and recognizable to most native speakers from elsewhere in Portugal).
       </li>
       <li>
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Loudspeaker.svg">
         <img alt="Loudspeaker.svg" data-file-height="20" data-file-width="20" height="11" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" width="11"/>
        </a>

        <a href="/wiki/Madeira" title="Madeira">

        </a>
        .
       </li>

        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Loudspeaker.svg">

        <a href="/wiki/Porto" title="Porto">

        </a>

        <a href="/wiki/Aveiro,_Portugal" title="Aveiro, Portugal">

        </a>
        .
       </li>

          Transmontano
         </i>
        </a>
        —
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tr%C3%A1s-os-Montes_e_Alto_Douro" title="Trás-os-Montes e Alto Douro">

        </a>
        .
       </li>

        </a>

         <i>
          Timorense
         </i>
        </a>
        (
        <a href="/wiki/East_Timorese_Portuguese" title="East Timorese Portuguese">
         East Timorese Portuguese
        </a>
        )
       </li>
       <li>
        <span class="flagicon">
         <img alt="" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="900" data-file-width="1350" height="15" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/4/41/Flag_of_India.svg/23px-Flag_of_India.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/4/41/Flag_of_India.svg/35px-Flag_of_India.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/4/41/Flag_of_India.svg/45px-Flag_of_India.svg.png 2x" width="23"/>

        (
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Damanese_Portuguese" title="Damanese Portuguese">

        </i>
        (
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Goan_Portuguese" title="Goan Portuguese">

        </a>
        )
       </li>
       <li>
        <span class="flagicon">

        </span>
        <a href="/wiki/Guinea-Bissau" title="Guinea-Bissau">
         Guinea-Bissau
        </a>
        —
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Loudspeaker.svg">

        </a>
        <a class="external text" href="http://cvc.instituto-camoes.pt/hlp/geografia/som88.html" rel="nofollow">

        <a href="/wiki/Guinean_Portuguese" title="Guinean Portuguese">

       <li>
        <span class="flagicon">

        </span>

        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Loudspeaker.svg">

        </a>
        <a class="external text" href="http://cvc.instituto-camoes.pt/hlp/geografia/som92.html" rel="nofollow">
         <i>
          Macaense
         </i>
        </a>
        (
        <a href="/wiki/Macanese_Portuguese" title="Macanese Portuguese">
         Macanese Portuguese
        </a>
        )
       </li>
       <li>
        <span class="flagicon">
         <img alt="" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="900" height="15" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/Flag_of_Mozambique.svg/23px-Flag_of_Mozambique.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/Flag_of_Mozambique.svg/35px-Flag_of_Mozambique.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/Flag_of_Mozambique.svg/45px-Flag_of_Mozambique.svg.png 2x" width="23"/>
        </span>
        <a href="/wiki/Mozambique" title="Mozambique">
         Mozambique
        </a>
        —
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Loudspeaker.svg">
         <img alt="Loudspeaker.svg" data-file-height="20" data-file-width="20" height="11" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" width="11"/>
        </a>
        <a class="external text" href="http://cvc.instituto-camoes.pt/hlp/geografia/som89.html" rel="nofollow">
         <i>
          Moçambicano
         </i>
        </a>
        (
        <a href="/wiki/Mozambican_Portuguese" title="Mozambican Portuguese">
         Mozambican Portuguese
        </a>
        )
       </li>
       <li>
        <span class="flagicon">
         <img alt="" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="1400" data-file-width="2800" height="12" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/Flag_of_Sao_Tome_and_Principe.svg/23px-Flag_of_Sao_Tome_and_Principe.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/Flag_of_Sao_Tome_and_Principe.svg/35px-Flag_of_Sao_Tome_and_Principe.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/Flag_of_Sao_Tome_and_Principe.svg/46px-Flag_of_Sao_Tome_and_Principe.svg.png 2x" width="23"/>
        </span>
        <a href="/wiki/S%C3%A3o_Tom%C3%A9_and_Pr%C3%ADncipe" title="São Tomé and Príncipe">
         São Tomé and Príncipe
        </a>
        —
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Loudspeaker.svg">
         <img alt="Loudspeaker.svg" data-file-height="20" data-file-width="20" height="11" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" width="11"/>
        </a>
        <a class="external text" href="http://cvc.instituto-camoes.pt/hlp/geografia/som83.html" rel="nofollow">
         <i>
          Santomense
         </i>
        </a>
        (
        <a href="/wiki/S%C3%A3o_Tomean_Portuguese" title="São Tomean Portuguese">
         São Tomean Portuguese
        </a>
        )
       </li>
       <li>
        <span class="flagicon">
         <img alt="" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="500" data-file-width="750" height="15" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/9a/Flag_of_Spain.svg/23px-Flag_of_Spain.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/9a/Flag_of_Spain.svg/35px-Flag_of_Spain.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/9a/Flag_of_Spain.svg/45px-Flag_of_Spain.svg.png 2x" width="23"/>
        </span>
        <a href="/wiki/Spain" title="Spain">
         Spain
        </a>
        —
        <a href="/wiki/Alentejan_Portuguese" title="Alentejan Portuguese">
         Oliventian Portuguese
        </a>
        and other varieties sometimes controversially deemed as separate languages, such as
        <a href="/wiki/Galician_language" title="Galician language">
         Galician
        </a>
        and
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Fala_language" title="Fala language">
          Fala
         </a>
        </i>
        .
       </li>
       <li>
        <span class="flagicon">
         <img alt="" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="900" height="15" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Flag_of_Uruguay.svg/23px-Flag_of_Uruguay.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Flag_of_Uruguay.svg/35px-Flag_of_Uruguay.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Flag_of_Uruguay.svg/45px-Flag_of_Uruguay.svg.png 2x" width="23"/>
        </span>
        <a href="/wiki/Uruguay" title="Uruguay">
         Uruguay
        </a>
        —
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Riverense_Portu%C3%B1ol_language" title="Riverense Portuñol language">
         <i>
          Dialectos Portugueses del Uruguay (DPU)
         </i>
        </a>
       </li>
      </ul>
      <p>
       Differences between dialects are mostly of
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Accent_(dialect)" title="Accent (dialect)">
        accent
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Vocabulary" title="Vocabulary">
        vocabulary
       </a>
       , but between the Brazilian dialects and other dialects, especially in their most colloquial forms, there can also be some grammatical differences. The
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Portuguese_creole" title="Portuguese creole">
        Portuguese-based creoles
       </a>
       spoken in various parts of Africa, Asia, and the Americas are independent languages.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Characterization_and_peculiarities">
        Characterization and peculiarities
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Portuguese_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Characterization and peculiarities">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       Portuguese, like
       <a href="/wiki/Catalan_language" title="Catalan language">
        Catalan
       </a>
       , preserved the stressed vowels of
       <a href="/wiki/Vulgar_Latin" title="Vulgar Latin">
        Vulgar Latin
       </a>
       , which became diphthongs in most other Romance languages; cf. Port., Cat., Sard.
       <i>
        <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/pedra" title="wikt:pedra">
         pedra
        </a>
       </i>
       ; Fr.
       <i>
        <span lang="fr">
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/pierre#French" title="wikt:pierre">
          pierre
         </a>
        </span>
       </i>
       , Sp.
       <i>
        <span lang="es">
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/piedra#Spanish" title="wikt:piedra">
          piedra
         </a>
        </span>
       </i>
       , It.
       <i>
        <span lang="it">
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/pietra#Italian" title="wikt:pietra">
          pietra
         </a>
        </span>
       </i>
       , Ro.
       <i>
        <span lang="ro">
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/piatr%C4%83#Romanian" title="wikt:piatră">
          piatră
         </a>
        </span>
       </i>
       , from Lat.
       <i>
        <span lang="la">
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/petra#Latin" title="wikt:petra">
          petra
         </a>
        </span>
       </i>
       ("stone"); or Port.
       <i>
        <span lang="pt">
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/fogo#Portuguese" title="wikt:fogo">
          fogo
         </a>
        </span>
       </i>
       , Cat.
       <i>
        <span lang="ca">
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/foc#Catalan" title="wikt:foc">
          foc
         </a>
        </span>
       </i>
       , Sard.
       <i>
        <span lang="sc">
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/fogu#Sardinian" title="wikt:fogu">
          fogu
         </a>
        </span>
       </i>
       ; Sp.
       <i>
        <span lang="es">
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/fuego#Spanish" title="wikt:fuego">
          fuego
         </a>
        </span>
       </i>
       , It.
       <i>
        <span lang="it">
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/fuoco#Italian" title="wikt:fuoco">
          fuoco
         </a>
        </span>
       </i>
       , Fr.
       <i>
        <span lang="fr">
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/feu#French" title="wikt:feu">
          feu
         </a>
        </span>
       </i>
       , Ro.
       <i>
        <span lang="ro">
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/foc#Romanian" title="wikt:foc">
          foc
         </a>
        </span>
       </i>
       , from Lat.
       <i>
        <span lang="la">
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/focus#Latin" title="wikt:focus">
          focus
         </a>
        </span>
       </i>
       ("fire"). Another characteristic of early Portuguese was the loss of
       <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/intervocalic" title="wiktionary:intervocalic">
        intervocalic
       </a>
       <i>
        l
       </i>
       and
       <i>
        n
       </i>
       , sometimes followed by the merger of the two surrounding vowels, or by the insertion of an
       <a href="/wiki/Epenthesis" title="Epenthesis">
        epenthetic vowel
       </a>
       between them: cf. Lat.
       <i>
        <span lang="la">
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/salire#Latin" title="wikt:salire">
          salire
         </a>
        </span>
       </i>
       ("to jump"),
       <i>
        <span lang="la">
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/tenere#Latin" title="wikt:tenere">
          tenere
         </a>
        </span>
       </i>
       ("to hold"),
       <i>
        <span lang="la">
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/catena#Latin" title="wikt:catena">
          catena
         </a>
        </span>
       </i>
       ("chain"), Sp.
       <i>
        <span lang="es">
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/salir#Spanish" title="wikt:salir">
          salir
         </a>
        </span>
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        <span lang="es">
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/tener#Spanish" title="wikt:tener">
          tener
         </a>
        </span>
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        <span lang="es">
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/cadena#Spanish" title="wikt:cadena">
          cadena
         </a>
        </span>
       </i>
       , Port.
       <i>
        <span lang="pt">
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/sair#Portuguese" title="wikt:sair">
          sair
         </a>
        </span>
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        <span lang="pt">
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/ter#Portuguese" title="wikt:ter">
          ter
         </a>
        </span>
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        <span lang="pt">
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/cadeia#Portuguese" title="wikt:cadeia">
          cadeia
         </a>
        </span>
       </i>
       . This characteristic happens today in
       <a href="/wiki/Celtic_languages" title="Celtic languages">
        Celtic languages
       </a>
       , such as Irish and Scottish
       <a href="/wiki/Goidelic_languages" title="Goidelic languages">
        Gaelic
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80">
        <a href="#cite_note-80">
         [80]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       When the
       <a href="/wiki/Elision" title="Elision">
        elided
       </a>
       consonant was
       <i>
        n
       </i>
       , it often
       <a href="/wiki/Nasalization" title="Nasalization">
        nasalized
       </a>
       the preceding vowel: cf. Lat.
       <i>
        <span lang="la">
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/manum#Latin" title="wikt:manum">
          manum
         </a>
        </span>
       </i>
       ("hand"),
       <i>
        <span lang="la">
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/ranam#Latin" title="wikt:ranam">
          ranam
         </a>
        </span>
       </i>
       ("frog"),
       <i>
        <span lang="la">
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/bonum#Latin" title="wikt:bonum">
          bonum
         </a>
        </span>
       </i>
       ("good"), Port.
       <i>
        <span lang="pt">
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/m%C3%A3o#Portuguese" title="wikt:mão">
          mão
         </a>
        </span>
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        <span lang="pt">
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/r%C3%A3a#Portuguese" title="wikt:rãa">
          rãa
         </a>
        </span>
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        <span lang="pt">
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/b%C3%B5o#Portuguese" title="wikt:bõo">
          bõo
         </a>
        </span>
       </i>
       (now
       <i>
        <span lang="pt">
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/m%C3%A3o#Portuguese" title="wikt:mão">
          mão
         </a>
        </span>
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        <span lang="pt">
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/r%C3%A3#Portuguese" title="wikt:rã">
          rã
         </a>
        </span>
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        <span lang="pt">
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/bom#Portuguese" title="wikt:bom">
          bom
         </a>
        </span>
       </i>
       ). This process was the source of most of the language's distinctive nasal diphthongs. In particular, the Latin endings
       <i>
        <span lang="la">
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/-anem#Latin" title="wikt:-anem">
          -anem
         </a>
        </span>
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        <span lang="la">
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/-anum#Latin" title="wikt:-anum">
          -anum
         </a>
        </span>
       </i>
       and
       <i>
        <span lang="la">
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/-onem#Latin" title="wikt:-onem">
          -onem
         </a>
        </span>
       </i>
       became
       <i>
        <span lang="pt">
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/-%C3%A3o#Portuguese" title="wikt:-ão">
          -ão
         </a>
        </span>
       </i>
       in most cases, cf. Lat.
       <i>
        <span lang="la">
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/canis#Latin" title="wikt:canis">
          canis
         </a>
        </span>
       </i>
       ("dog"),
       <i>
        <span lang="la">
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/germanus#Latin" title="wikt:germanus">
          germanus
         </a>
        </span>
       </i>
       ("brother"),
       <i>
        <span lang="la">
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/ratio#Latin" title="wikt:ratio">
          ratio
         </a>
        </span>
       </i>
       ("reason") with Modern Port.
       <i>
        <span lang="pt">
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/c%C3%A3o#Portuguese" title="wikt:cão">
          cão
         </a>
        </span>
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        <span lang="pt">
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/irm%C3%A3o#Portuguese" title="wikt:irmão">
          irmão
         </a>
        </span>
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        <span lang="pt">
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/raz%C3%A3o#Portuguese" title="wikt:razão">
          razão
         </a>
        </span>
       </i>
       , and their plurals
       <i>
        -anes
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        -anos
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        -ones
       </i>
       normally became
       <i>
        -ães
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        -ãos
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        -ões
       </i>
       , cf.
       <i>
        cães
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        irmãos
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        razões
       </i>
       . This nasalisation could be an ancient
       <a href="/wiki/Proto-Celtic_language" title="Proto-Celtic language">
        Proto-Celtic
       </a>
       characteristic which also exists today in
       <a href="/wiki/Breton_language" title="Breton language">
        Breton
       </a>
       and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gaelic_language" title="Gaelic language">
        Gaelic
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81">
        <a href="#cite_note-81">
         [81]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The Portuguese language is also the only
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Romance_language" title="Romance language">
        Romance language
       </a>
       that has preserved the clitic case
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mesoclisis" title="Mesoclisis">
        mesoclisis
       </a>
       : cf.
       <i>
        <span lang="pt">
         dar-te-ei
        </span>
       </i>
       (I'll give thee),
       <i>
        <span lang="pt">
         amar-te-ei
        </span>
       </i>
       (I'll love you),
       <i>
        <span lang="pt">
         contactá-los-ei
        </span>
       </i>
       (I'll contact them). It was also the only Western Romance language to retain the Latin synthetic
       <a href="/wiki/Pluperfect" title="Pluperfect">
        pluperfect
       </a>
       tense:
       <i>
        <span lang="pt">
         eu estivera
        </span>
       </i>
       (I had been),
       <i>
        <span lang="pt">
         eu vivera
        </span>
       </i>
       (I had lived),
       <i>
        <span lang="pt">
         vós vivêreis
        </span>
       </i>
       (you had lived).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82">
        <a href="#cite_note-82">
         [82]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <a href="/wiki/Romanian_language" title="Romanian language">
        Romanian
       </a>
       also has this tense, but uses the -s- form.
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Vocabulary">
        Vocabulary
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Portuguese_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Vocabulary">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_vocabulary" title="Portuguese vocabulary">
        Portuguese vocabulary
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Biblioteca_nacional_rio_janeiro.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2153" data-file-width="3229" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/Biblioteca_nacional_rio_janeiro.jpg/220px-Biblioteca_nacional_rio_janeiro.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/Biblioteca_nacional_rio_janeiro.jpg/330px-Biblioteca_nacional_rio_janeiro.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/Biblioteca_nacional_rio_janeiro.jpg/440px-Biblioteca_nacional_rio_janeiro.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Biblioteca_nacional_rio_janeiro.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         The
         <a href="/wiki/National_Library_of_Brazil" title="National Library of Brazil">
          National Library of Brazil
         </a>
         , in
         <a href="/wiki/Rio_de_Janeiro" title="Rio de Janeiro">
          Rio de Janeiro
         </a>
         , the largest library in
         <a href="/wiki/Latin_America" title="Latin America">
          Latin America
         </a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:CoimbraUniLibrary-CCSA.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="450" height="293" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/CoimbraUniLibrary-CCSA.jpg/220px-CoimbraUniLibrary-CCSA.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/CoimbraUniLibrary-CCSA.jpg/330px-CoimbraUniLibrary-CCSA.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/CoimbraUniLibrary-CCSA.jpg/440px-CoimbraUniLibrary-CCSA.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:CoimbraUniLibrary-CCSA.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Baroque Library of the
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Coimbra_University" title="Coimbra University">
          Coimbra University
         </a>
         , Portugal
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:RealGabinetePortuguesLeitura1.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="873" data-file-width="768" height="250" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/RealGabinetePortuguesLeitura1.jpg/220px-RealGabinetePortuguesLeitura1.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/RealGabinetePortuguesLeitura1.jpg/330px-RealGabinetePortuguesLeitura1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/RealGabinetePortuguesLeitura1.jpg/440px-RealGabinetePortuguesLeitura1.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:RealGabinetePortuguesLeitura1.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         The Royal Portuguese Reading Room in
         <a href="/wiki/Rio_de_Janeiro" title="Rio de Janeiro">
          Rio de Janeiro
         </a>
         , Brazil
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Macau_Museum_Inside.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1460" data-file-width="3242" height="99" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/Macau_Museum_Inside.jpg/220px-Macau_Museum_Inside.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/Macau_Museum_Inside.jpg/330px-Macau_Museum_Inside.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/Macau_Museum_Inside.jpg/440px-Macau_Museum_Inside.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Macau_Museum_Inside.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         A sign in the
         <a href="/wiki/Museum_of_Macau" title="Museum of Macau">
          Museum of Macau
         </a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Most of the lexicon of Portuguese is derived, directly or through other Romance languages, from Latin. Nevertheless, because of its original
       <a href="/wiki/Celtiberian_language" title="Celtiberian language">
        Celtiberian
       </a>
       heritage and later the participation of Portugal in the
       <a href="/wiki/Age_of_Discovery" title="Age of Discovery">
        Age of Discovery
       </a>
       , it has some
       <a href="/wiki/Gallaecian_language" title="Gallaecian language">
        Gallaecian
       </a>
       words and adopted
       <a href="/wiki/Loanword" title="Loanword">
        loanwords
       </a>
       from all over the world.
      </p>
      <p>
       A number of Portuguese words can still be traced to the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pre-Roman_peoples_of_the_Iberian_Peninsula" title="Pre-Roman peoples of the Iberian Peninsula">
        pre-Roman inhabitants of Portugal
       </a>
       , which included the
       <a href="/wiki/Gallaeci" title="Gallaeci">
        Gallaeci
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Lusitanians" title="Lusitanians">
        Lusitanians
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Celtici" title="Celtici">
        Celtici
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Cynetes" title="Cynetes">
        Cynetes
       </a>
       . Most of these words derived from
       <a href="/wiki/Celtic_languages" title="Celtic languages">
        Celtic
       </a>
       and are very often shared with
       <a href="/wiki/Galician_language" title="Galician language">
        Galician
       </a>
       since both languages share a common origin in the medieval language of Galician-Portuguese. A few of these words existed in Latin as loanwords from a
       <a href="/wiki/Celtic_languages" title="Celtic languages">
        Celtic
       </a>
       source, often
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gaulish" title="Gaulish">
        Gaulish
       </a>
       . Altogether these are over 1,000 words, some verbs and toponymic names of towns, rivers, utensils and plants.
      </p>
      <p>
       In the 5th century, the Iberian Peninsula (the
       <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Rome" title="Ancient Rome">
        Roman
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Hispania" title="Hispania">
        Hispania
       </a>
       ) was conquered by the
       <a href="/wiki/Germanic_peoples" title="Germanic peoples">
        Germanic
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Suebi" title="Suebi">
        Suebi
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Visigoths" title="Visigoths">
        Visigoths
       </a>
       . As they adopted the Roman civilization and language, however, these people contributed with some 500
       <a href="/wiki/Germanic_languages" title="Germanic languages">
        Germanic
       </a>
       words to the lexicon. Many of these words are related to warfare—such as
       <i>
        espora
       </i>
       "spur",
       <i>
        estaca
       </i>
       "stake", and
       <i>
        guerra
       </i>
       "war", from
       <a href="/wiki/Gothic_language" title="Gothic language">
        Gothic
       </a>
       <i>
        *spaúra
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        *stakka
       </i>
       , and
       <i>
        *wirro
       </i>
       , respectively. The
       <a href="/wiki/Germanic_languages" title="Germanic languages">
        Germanic languages
       </a>
       influence also exists in
       <a href="/wiki/Toponymic_surname" title="Toponymic surname">
        toponymic surnames
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Patronymic_surname" title="Patronymic surname">
        patronymic surnames
       </a>
       borne by Visigoth sovereigns and their descendants, and it dwells on placenames such has
       <a href="/wiki/Ermesinde" title="Ermesinde">
        Ermesinde
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Esposende" title="Esposende">
        Esposende
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Resende,_Portugal" title="Resende, Portugal">
        Resende
       </a>
       where
       <i>
        sinde
       </i>
       and
       <i>
        sende
       </i>
       are derived from the Germanic "sinths" (military expedition) and in the case of Resende, the prefix
       <i>
        re
       </i>
       comes from Germanic "reths" (council). Other examples of Portuguese names, surnames and town names of Germanic
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Toponymic" title="Toponymic">
        toponymic
       </a>
       origin include Henrique,
       <a href="/wiki/Henriques_(surname)" title="Henriques (surname)">
        Henriques
       </a>
       , Vermoim, Mandim, Calquim, Baguim, Gemunde, Guetim, Sermonde and many more, are quite common mainly in the old
       <a href="/wiki/Suebi" title="Suebi">
        Suebi
       </a>
       and later
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Visigothic" title="Visigothic">
        Visigothic
       </a>
       dominated regions, covering today's Northern half of Portugal and
       <a href="/wiki/Galicia_(Spain)" title="Galicia (Spain)">
        Galicia
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       Between the 9th and early 13th centuries, Portuguese acquired nearly 800 words from
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Arabic_language" title="Arabic language">
        Arabic
       </a>
       by influence of
       <a href="/wiki/Al-Andalus" title="Al-Andalus">
        Moorish Iberia
       </a>
       . They are often recognizable by the initial
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Definite_article_in_Arabic" title="Definite article in Arabic">
        Arabic article
        <i>
         a(l)-
        </i>
       </a>
       , and include many common words such as
       <i>
        aldeia
       </i>
       "village" from الضيعة
       <i>
        alḍai`a
       </i>
       (or from
       <a href="/wiki/Edictum_Rothari" title="Edictum Rothari">
        Edictum Rothari
       </a>
       :
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Aldii" title="Aldii">
         aldii
        </a>
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        aldias
       </i>
       ),
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83">
        <a href="#cite_note-83">
         [83]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <i>
        alface
       </i>
       "lettuce" from الخس
       <i>
        alkhass
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        armazém
       </i>
       "warehouse" from المخزن
       <i>
        almakhzan
       </i>
       , and
       <i>
        azeite
       </i>
       "olive oil" from الزيت
       <i>
        azzait
       </i>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       Starting in the 15th century, the Portuguese maritime explorations led to the introduction of many loanwords from Asian languages. For instance,
       <i>
        catana
       </i>
       "cutlass" from
       <a href="/wiki/Japanese_language" title="Japanese language">
        Japanese
       </a>
       <i>
        katana
       </i>
       and
       <i>
        chá
       </i>
       "tea" from
       <a href="/wiki/Chinese_language" title="Chinese language">
        Chinese
       </a>
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Tea#Etymology" title="Tea">
         <i>
          chá
         </i>
        </a>
       </i>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       From the 16th to the 19th centuries, because of the role of Portugal as intermediary in the
       <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_slave_trade" title="Atlantic slave trade">
        Atlantic slave trade
       </a>
       , and the establishment of large Portuguese colonies in Angola, Mozambique, and Brazil, Portuguese acquired several words of African and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Indigenous_peoples_of_Brazil" title="Indigenous peoples of Brazil">
        Amerind
       </a>
       origin, especially names for most of the animals and plants found in those territories. While those terms are mostly used in the former colonies, many became current in European Portuguese as well. From
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kimbundu_language" title="Kimbundu language">
        Kimbundu
       </a>
       , for example, came
       <i>
        kifumate
       </i>
       &gt;
       <i>
        cafuné
       </i>
       "head caress" (Brazil),
       <i>
        kusula
       </i>
       &gt;
       <i>
        caçula
       </i>
       "youngest child" (Brazil),
       <i>
        marimbondo
       </i>
       "tropical wasp" (Brazil), and
       <i>
        kubungula
       </i>
       &gt;
       <i>
        bungular
       </i>
       "to dance like a wizard" (Angola). From South America came
       <i>
        batata
       </i>
       "
       <a href="/wiki/Potato" title="Potato">
        potato
       </a>
       ", from
       <a href="/wiki/Ta%C3%ADno_language" title="Taíno language">
        Taino
       </a>
       ;
       <i>
        ananás
       </i>
       and
       <i>
        abacaxi
       </i>
       , from
       <a href="/wiki/Tupi%E2%80%93Guarani_languages" title="Tupi–Guarani languages">
        Tupi–Guarani
       </a>
       <i>
        naná
       </i>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Tupi_language" title="Tupi language">
        Tupi
       </a>
       <i>
        ibá cati
       </i>
       , respectively (two species of
       <a href="/wiki/Pineapple" title="Pineapple">
        pineapple
       </a>
       ), and
       <i>
        pipoca
       </i>
       "
       <a href="/wiki/Popcorn" title="Popcorn">
        popcorn
       </a>
       " from
       <a href="/wiki/Tupi_language" title="Tupi language">
        Tupi
       </a>
       and
       <i>
        tucano
       </i>
       "
       <a href="/wiki/Toucan" title="Toucan">
        toucan
       </a>
       " from
       <a href="/wiki/Guarani_language" title="Guarani language">
        Guarani
       </a>
       <i>
        tucan
       </i>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       Finally, it has received a steady influx of loanwords from other European languages, especially French and
       <a href="/wiki/English_language" title="English language">
        English
       </a>
       . These are by far the most important languages when referring to loanwords. There are many examples such as:
       <i>
        colchete
       </i>
       /
       <i>
        crochê
       </i>
       "bracket"/"crochet",
       <i>
        paletó
       </i>
       "jacket",
       <i>
        batom
       </i>
       "lipstick", and
       <i>
        filé
       </i>
       /
       <i>
        filete
       </i>
       "steak"/"slice",
       <i>
        rua
       </i>
       "street" respectively, from French
       <i>
        crochet
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        paletot
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        bâton
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        filet
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        rue
       </i>
       ; and
       <i>
        bife
       </i>
       "steak",
       <i>
        futebol
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        revólver
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        stock
       </i>
       /
       <i>
        estoque
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        folclore
       </i>
       , from English
       <i>
        beef
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        football
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        revolver
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        stock
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        folklore
       </i>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       Examples from other European languages:
       <i>
        macarrão
       </i>
       "pasta",
       <i>
        piloto
       </i>
       "pilot",
       <i>
        carroça
       </i>
       "carriage", and
       <i>
        barraca
       </i>
       "barrack", from Italian
       <i>
        maccherone
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        pilota
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        carrozza
       </i>
       , and
       <i>
        baracca
       </i>
       ;
       <i>
        melena
       </i>
       "hair lock",
       <i>
        fiambre
       </i>
       "wet-cured ham" (in Portugal, in contrast with
       <i>
        presunto
       </i>
       "dry-cured ham" from Latin
       <i>
        prae-exsuctus
       </i>
       "dehydrated") or "canned ham" (in Brazil, in contrast with non-canned, wet-cured
       <i>
        presunto cozido
       </i>
       and dry-cured
       <i>
        presunto cru
       </i>
       ), and
       <i>
        castelhano
       </i>
       "Castilian", from Spanish
       <i>
        melena
       </i>
       "mane",
       <i>
        fiambre
       </i>
       and
       <i>
        castellano
       </i>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       Before the last four decades, Brazilians adopted a greater number of loanwords from Japanese and other European languages (due to the
       <a href="/wiki/Immigration_to_Brazil" title="Immigration to Brazil">
        historical immigration
       </a>
       affecting their demographics), and they were and are also more willing to adopt foreign terms that come from
       <a href="/wiki/Globalization" title="Globalization">
        globalization
       </a>
       than the Portuguese, while the degree of African, Tupian and other Amerindian lexicon in Brazilian Portuguese is shown to be surprisingly lesser than that commonly expected of the said variant by the local Africanist and Indianist academia (that also has to some degree influenced the common sense of what gives a different cultural identity of Brazilians in relation to the Portuguese), so that its lexicon is almost identical (about 99%) to that of European Portuguese.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84">
        <a href="#cite_note-84">
         [84]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dummies_85-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-dummies-85">
         [85]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86">
        <a href="#cite_note-86">
         [86]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Many Portuguese settlers to Colonial Brazil were from northern and insular Portugal,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87">
        <a href="#cite_note-87">
         [87]
        </a>
       </sup>
       apart from some historically important
       <a href="/wiki/Illegal_immigration" title="Illegal immigration">
        illegal immigrants
       </a>
       from elsewhere in Europe, such as Galicia, France and the Netherlands.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88">
        <a href="#cite_note-88">
         [88]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Brazil received more European immigrants in its colonial history than the
       <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">
        United States
       </a>
       . Between 1500 and 1760, 700,000 Europeans (overwhelmingly Portuguese) settled in Brazil, while 530,000 Europeans settled in the United States for the same given time.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_89-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-89">
         [89]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Classification_and_related_languages">
        Classification and related languages
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Portuguese_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Classification and related languages">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:362px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Linguistic_map_Southwestern_Europe.gif">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="544" data-file-width="600" height="326" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4d/Linguistic_map_Southwestern_Europe.gif/360px-Linguistic_map_Southwestern_Europe.gif" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4d/Linguistic_map_Southwestern_Europe.gif/540px-Linguistic_map_Southwestern_Europe.gif 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/4/4d/Linguistic_map_Southwestern_Europe.gif 2x" width="360"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Linguistic_map_Southwestern_Europe.gif" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Map showing the historical retreat and expansion of Portuguese (
         <a href="/wiki/Galician-Portuguese" title="Galician-Portuguese">
          Galician-Portuguese
         </a>
         ) within the context of its linguistic neighbours between the year 1000 and 2000.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:322px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Lenguas_y_dialectos_iberorromances.PNG">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="720" data-file-width="820" height="281" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Lenguas_y_dialectos_iberorromances.PNG/320px-Lenguas_y_dialectos_iberorromances.PNG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Lenguas_y_dialectos_iberorromances.PNG/480px-Lenguas_y_dialectos_iberorromances.PNG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Lenguas_y_dialectos_iberorromances.PNG/640px-Lenguas_y_dialectos_iberorromances.PNG 2x" width="320"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Lenguas_y_dialectos_iberorromances.PNG" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Map showing mostly contemporary
         <a href="/wiki/West_Iberian_languages" title="West Iberian languages">
          West Iberian
         </a>
         and
         <a href="/wiki/Occitano-Romance_languages" title="Occitano-Romance languages">
          Occitano-Romance
         </a>
         languages, as well many of their mainland European dialects (take note that areas colored green,
         <a href="/wiki/Aragonese_language" title="Aragonese language">
          gold
         </a>
         or pink/purple represent languages deemed
         <a href="/wiki/Endangered_language" title="Endangered language">
          endangered
         </a>
         by UNESCO, so this may be outdated in less than a few decades). It shows European Portuguese,
         <a href="/wiki/Galician_language" title="Galician language">
          Galician
         </a>
         ,
         <a href="/wiki/Galician-Asturian" title="Galician-Asturian">
          Eonavian
         </a>
         ,
         <a href="/wiki/Mirandese_language" title="Mirandese language">
          Mirandese
         </a>
         and the
         <a href="/wiki/Fala_language" title="Fala language">
          Fala
         </a>
         as not only closely related but as
         <a href="/wiki/Dialect_continuum" title="Dialect continuum">
          dialect continuum
         </a>
         , though it excludes dialects spoken in insular Portugal (Azores and Madeira–
         <a href="/wiki/Canarian_Spanish" title="Canarian Spanish">
          Canaries
         </a>
         is not shown either).
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main articles:
       <a href="/wiki/Iberian_Romance_languages" title="Iberian Romance languages">
        Iberian Romance languages
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Galician-Portuguese" title="Galician-Portuguese">
        Galician-Portuguese
       </a>
       , and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Comparison_of_Spanish_and_Portuguese" title="Comparison of Spanish and Portuguese">
        Comparison of Spanish and Portuguese
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       Portuguese belongs to the
       <a href="/wiki/West_Iberian_languages" title="West Iberian languages">
        West Iberian
       </a>
       branch of the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Romance_language" title="Romance language">
        Romance languages
       </a>
       , and it has special ties with the following members of this group:
      </p>
      <ul>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Galician_language" title="Galician language">
         Galician
        </a>
        ,
        <a href="/wiki/Fala_language" title="Fala language">
         Fala
        </a>
        and
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Riverense_Portu%C3%B1ol_language" title="Riverense Portuñol language">
         <i>
          portunhol do pampa
         </i>
        </a>
        (the way
        <i>
         riverense
        </i>
        and its sibling dialects are referred to in Portuguese), its closest relatives.
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Mirandese_language" title="Mirandese language">
         Mirandese
        </a>
        ,
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Leonese_language" title="Leonese language">
         Leonese
        </a>
        ,
        <a href="/wiki/Asturian_language" title="Asturian language">
         Asturian
        </a>
        ,
        <a href="/wiki/Extremaduran_language" title="Extremaduran language">
         Extremaduran
        </a>
        and
        <a href="/wiki/Cantabrian_dialect" title="Cantabrian dialect">
         Cantabrian
        </a>
        (
        <a href="/wiki/Astur-Leonese_languages" title="Astur-Leonese languages">
         Astur-Leonese languages
        </a>
        ). Mirandese is the only recognised regional language spoken in Portugal (beside Portuguese, the only official language in Portugal).
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Spanish_language" title="Spanish language">
         Spanish
        </a>
        and
        <a href="/wiki/Cal%C3%B3_language" title="Caló language">
         <i>
          calão
         </i>
        </a>
        (the way
        <i>
         caló
        </i>
        , language of the Iberian
        <a href="/wiki/Romani_people" title="Romani people">
         Romani
        </a>
        , is referred to in Portuguese).
       </li>
      </ul>
      <p>
       Portuguese and other Romance languages (namely French and Italian) are not mutually intelligible, although they share considerable similarities in both vocabulary and grammar. Portuguese speakers will usually need some formal study before attaining strong comprehension in those Romance languages, and vice versa. However, Portuguese and Galician are mutually intelligible. Given that Portuguese has a larger phonemic inventory than Spanish, Portuguese is only moderately intelligible to some Spanish speakers, despite the strong lexical and grammatical similarity (89%) between the two.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90">
        <a href="#cite_note-90">
         [90]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91">
        <a href="#cite_note-91">
         [91]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92">
        <a href="#cite_note-92">
         [92]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93">
        <a href="#cite_note-93">
         [93]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       <a href="/wiki/Portu%C3%B1ol" title="Portuñol">
        <i>
         Portunhol
        </i>
       </a>
       , a form of
       <a href="/wiki/Code-switching" title="Code-switching">
        code-switching
       </a>
       , has a more lively use and is more readily mentioned in popular culture in South America. Said code-switching is not to be confused with the
       <i>
        portunhol
       </i>
       spoken on the borders of Brazil with Uruguay (
       <i>
        <span lang="pt">
         <i>
          dialeto do pampa
         </i>
        </span>
       </i>
       ) and Paraguay (
       <i>
        <span lang="pt">
         <i>
          dialeto dos
          <a href="/wiki/Brasiguayos" title="Brasiguayos">
           brasiguaios
          </a>
         </i>
        </span>
       </i>
       ), and of Portugal with Spain (
       <i>
        <span lang="pt">
         <i>
          <a href="/wiki/Barranquenho" title="Barranquenho">
           barranquenho
          </a>
         </i>
        </span>
       </i>
       ), that are Portuguese dialects spoken natively by thousands of people, which have been heavily influenced by Spanish.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lipski_94-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Lipski-94">
         [94]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Portuguese and Spanish are the only Ibero-Romance languages, and perhaps the only Romance languages with such thriving inter-language forms, in which visible and lively bilingual contact dialects and code-switching have formed, in which functional bilingual communication is achieved through attempting an approximation to the target foreign language (known as 'Portunhol') without a learned acquisition process, but nevertheless facilitates communication. There is an emerging literature focused on such phenomena (including informal attempts of standardization of the linguistic continua and their usage).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lipski_94-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-Lipski-94">
         [94]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Galician-Portuguese_in_Spain">
        Galician-Portuguese in Spain
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Portuguese_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Galician-Portuguese in Spain">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       See also:
       <a href="/wiki/Reintegrationism" title="Reintegrationism">
        Reintegrationism
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       The closest relative of Portuguese is Galician, which is spoken in the autonomous community (region) of
       <a href="/wiki/Galicia_(Spain)" title="Galicia (Spain)">
        Galicia
       </a>
       (northwestern Spain). The two were at one time a single language, known today as
       <a href="/wiki/Galician-Portuguese" title="Galician-Portuguese">
        Galician-Portuguese
       </a>
       , but they have diverged especially in pronunciation and vocabulary due to the political separation of Portugal from Galicia. There is, however, still a linguistic continuity consisting of the variant of Galician referred to as
       <i>
        galego-português baixo-limiao
       </i>
       , which is spoken in several Galician villages between the municipalities of
       <a href="/wiki/Entrimo" title="Entrimo">
        Entrimo
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Lobios" title="Lobios">
        Lobios
       </a>
       and the transborder region of the
       <a href="/wiki/Peneda-Ger%C3%AAs_National_Park" title="Peneda-Gerês National Park">
        natural park of Peneda-Gerês/Xurês
       </a>
       . It is "considered a rarity, a living vestige of the medieval language that ranged from
       <a href="/wiki/Cantabria" title="Cantabria">
        Cantabria
       </a>
       to
       <a href="/wiki/Mondego_River" title="Mondego River">
        Mondego
       </a>
       [...]".
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-agal-gz.or_95-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-agal-gz.or-95">
         [95]
        </a>
       </sup>
       As reported by UNESCO, due to the pressure of the Spanish language on the standard official version of the Galician language, the Galician language was on the verge of disappearing.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-agal-gz.or_95-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-agal-gz.or-95">
         [95]
        </a>
       </sup>
       According to the Unesco philologist Tapani Salminen, the proximity to Portuguese protects Galician.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96">
        <a href="#cite_note-96">
         [96]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Nevertheless, the core vocabulary and grammar of Galician are still noticeably closer to Portuguese than to those of Spanish. In particular, like Portuguese, it uses the future subjunctive, the personal infinitive, and the synthetic pluperfect. Mutual intelligibility (estimated at 90% by R. A. Hall, Jr., 1989)
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97">
        <a href="#cite_note-97">
         [97]
        </a>
       </sup>
       is excellent between Galicians and northern Portuguese. Many linguists consider
       <a href="/wiki/Galician_language" title="Galician language">
        Galician
       </a>
       to be a co-dialect of the Portuguese language.
      </p>
      <p>
       Another member of the Galician-Portuguese group, most commonly thought of as a Galician dialect, is spoken in the
       <a href="/wiki/Galician-Asturian" title="Galician-Asturian">
        Eonavian
       </a>
       region in a western strip in
       <a href="/wiki/Asturias" title="Asturias">
        Asturias
       </a>
       and the westernmost parts of the provinces of
       <a href="/wiki/Province_of_Le%C3%B3n" title="Province of León">
        León
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Province_of_Zamora" title="Province of Zamora">
        Zamora
       </a>
       , along the frontier with Galicia, between the
       <a href="/wiki/Eo_(river)" title="Eo (river)">
        Eo
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Navia_(river)" title="Navia (river)">
        Navia
       </a>
       rivers (or more exactly Eo and Frexulfe rivers). It is called
       <i>
        eonaviego
       </i>
       or
       <i>
        gallego-asturiano
       </i>
       by its speakers.
      </p>
      <p>
       The Fala language, known by its speakers as
       <i>
        xalimés
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        mañegu
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        a fala de Xálima
       </i>
       and
       <i>
        chapurráu
       </i>
       and in Portuguese as
       <i>
        a fala de Xálima
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        a fala da Estremadura
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        o galego da Estremadura
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        valego
       </i>
       ou
       <i>
        galaico-estremenho
       </i>
       , is another descendant of Galician-Portuguese, spoken by a small number of people in the Spanish towns of
       <a href="/wiki/Valverde_del_Fresno" title="Valverde del Fresno">
        Valverde del Fresno
       </a>
       (
       <i>
        Valverdi du Fresnu
       </i>
       ),
       <a href="/wiki/Eljas" title="Eljas">
        Eljas
       </a>
       (
       <i>
        As Ellas
       </i>
       ) and
       <a href="/wiki/San_Mart%C3%ADn_de_Trevejo" title="San Martín de Trevejo">
        San Martín de Trevejo
       </a>
       (
       <i>
        Sa Martín de Trevellu
       </i>
       ) in the autonomous community of
       <a href="/wiki/Extremadura" title="Extremadura">
        Extremadura
       </a>
       , near the border with Portugal.
      </p>
      <p>
       There are a number of other places in Spain in which the native language of the common people is a descendant of the Galician-Portuguese group, such as
       <a href="/wiki/La_Alamedilla" title="La Alamedilla">
        La Alamedilla
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Cedillo" title="Cedillo">
        Cedillo
       </a>
       (
       <i>
        Cedilho
       </i>
       ),
       <a href="/wiki/Herrera_de_Alc%C3%A1ntara" title="Herrera de Alcántara">
        Herrera de Alcántara
       </a>
       (
       <i>
        Ferreira d'Alcântara
       </i>
       ) and
       <a href="/wiki/Olivenza" title="Olivenza">
        Olivenza
       </a>
       (
       <i>
        Olivença
       </i>
       ), but in these municipalities, what is spoken is actually Portuguese, not disputed as such in the mainstream.
      </p>
      <p>
       It should be noticed that the diversity of dialects of the Portuguese language is known since the time of medieval Portuguese-Galician language when it coexisted with the Lusitanian-Mozarabic dialect, spoken in the south of Portugal. The dialectal diversity becomes more evident in the work of Fernão d'Oliveira, in the
       <b>
        Grammatica da Lingoagem Portuguesa
       </b>
       , (1536), where he remarks that the people of Portuguese regions of Beira, Alentejo, Estremadura, and Entre Douro e Minho, all speak differently from each other. Also Contador d'Argote (1725) distinguishes three main varieties of dialects: the local dialects, the dialects of time, and of profession (work jargon). Of local dialects he highlights five main dialects: the dialect of Estremadura, of Entre-Douro e Minho, of Beira, of Algarve and of Trás-os-Montes. He also makes reference to the overseas dialects, the rustic dialects, the poetic dialect and that of prose.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98">
        <a href="#cite_note-98">
         [98]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       In the kingdom of Portugal,
       <i>
        Ladinho
       </i>
       (or
       <i>
        Lingoagem Ladinha
       </i>
       ) was the name given to the pure Portuguese language romance, without any mixture of Aravia or Gerigonça Judenga.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99">
        <a href="#cite_note-99">
         [99]
        </a>
       </sup>
       While the term
       <i>
        língua vulgar
       </i>
       was used to name the language before D. Dinis decided to call it "Portuguese language",
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100">
        <a href="#cite_note-100">
         [100]
        </a>
       </sup>
       the erudite version used and known as Galician-Portuguese (the language of the Portuguese court) and all other Portuguese dialects were spoken at the same time. In a historical perspective the Portuguese language was never just one dialect. Just like today there is a standard Portuguese (actually two) among the several dialects of Portuguese, in the past there was Galician-Portuguese as the "standard", coexisting with other dialects.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Influence_on_other_languages">
        Influence on other languages
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Portuguese_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Influence on other languages">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       See also:
       <a href="/wiki/List_of_English_words_of_Portuguese_origin" title="List of English words of Portuguese origin">
        List of English words of Portuguese origin
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Loan_words_in_Malayalam#Portuguese" title="Loan words in Malayalam">
        Loan words in Malayalam § Portuguese
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Loan_words_in_Indonesian" title="Loan words in Indonesian">
        Loan words in Indonesian
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Japanese_words_of_Portuguese_origin" title="Japanese words of Portuguese origin">
        Japanese words of Portuguese origin
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_Malay_loanwords" title="List of Malay loanwords">
        List of Malay loanwords
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Portuguese_loanwords_in_Sinhala" title="Portuguese loanwords in Sinhala">
        Portuguese loanwords in Sinhala
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Loan_words_in_Sri_Lankan_Tamil#Portuguese" title="Loan words in Sri Lankan Tamil">
        Loan words in Sri Lankan Tamil § Portuguese
       </a>
       , and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sri_Lanka_Indo-Portuguese_language" title="Sri Lanka Indo-Portuguese language">
        Sri Lanka Indo-Portuguese language
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       Portuguese has provided
       <a href="/wiki/Loanword" title="Loanword">
        loanwords
       </a>
       to many languages, such as
       <a href="/wiki/Indonesian_language" title="Indonesian language">
        Indonesian
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Manado_Malay" title="Manado Malay">
        Manado Malay
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Malayalam" title="Malayalam">
        Malayalam
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sri_Lanka_Tamils_(native)" title="Sri Lanka Tamils (native)">
        Sri Lankan Tamil
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Sinhalese_language" title="Sinhalese language">
        Sinhalese
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Malay_language" title="Malay language">
        Malay
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Bengali_language" title="Bengali language">
        Bengali
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/English_(language)" title="English (language)">
        English
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Hindi" title="Hindi">
        Hindi
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Swahili_language" title="Swahili language">
        Swahili
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Afrikaans" title="Afrikaans">
        Afrikaans
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Konkani_language" title="Konkani language">
        Konkani
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Marathi_language" title="Marathi language">
        Marathi
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Tetum_language" title="Tetum language">
        Tetum
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Tsonga_language" title="Tsonga language">
        Xitsonga
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Japanese_language" title="Japanese language">
        Japanese
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Lanc-Patu%C3%A1_creole" title="Lanc-Patuá creole">
        Lanc-Patuá
       </a>
       (spoken in northern Brazil),
       <a href="/wiki/Esan_people#Language" title="Esan people">
        Esan
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Sranan_Tongo" title="Sranan Tongo">
        Sranan Tongo
       </a>
       (spoken in Suriname). It left a strong influence on the
       <i>
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Old_Tupi" title="Old Tupi">
         língua brasílica
        </a>
       </i>
       , a
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tupi%E2%80%93Guarani_language" title="Tupi–Guarani language">
        Tupi–Guarani language
       </a>
       , which was the most widely spoken in Brazil until the 18th century, and on the language spoken around
       <a href="/wiki/Sikka_Regency" title="Sikka Regency">
        Sikka
       </a>
       in
       <a href="/wiki/Flores" title="Flores">
        Flores
       </a>
       Island,
       <a href="/wiki/Indonesia" title="Indonesia">
        Indonesia
       </a>
       . In nearby
       <a href="/wiki/Larantuka" title="Larantuka">
        Larantuka
       </a>
       , Portuguese is used for prayers in
       <a href="/wiki/Holy_Week" title="Holy Week">
        Holy Week
       </a>
       rituals. The Japanese–Portuguese dictionary
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Nippo_Jisho" title="Nippo Jisho">
         Nippo Jisho
        </a>
       </i>
       (1603) was the first dictionary of Japanese in a European language, a product of
       <a href="/wiki/Society_of_Jesus" title="Society of Jesus">
        Jesuit
       </a>
       missionary activity in Japan. Building on the work of earlier Portuguese missionaries, the
       <i>
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dictionarium_Anamiticum,_Lusitanum_et_Latinum" title="Dictionarium Anamiticum, Lusitanum et Latinum">
         Dictionarium Anamiticum, Lusitanum et Latinum
        </a>
       </i>
       (Annamite–Portuguese–Latin dictionary) of
       <a href="/wiki/Alexandre_de_Rhodes" title="Alexandre de Rhodes">
        Alexandre de Rhodes
       </a>
       (1651) introduced the modern
       <a href="/wiki/Vietnamese_alphabet" title="Vietnamese alphabet">
        orthography of Vietnamese
       </a>
       , which is based on the orthography of 17th-century Portuguese. The
       <a href="/wiki/Romanization" title="Romanization">
        Romanization
       </a>
       of
       <a href="/wiki/Chinese_language" title="Chinese language">
        Chinese
       </a>
       was also influenced by the Portuguese language (among others), particularly regarding
       <a href="/wiki/List_of_common_Chinese_surnames" title="List of common Chinese surnames">
        Chinese surnames
       </a>
       ; one example is
       <i>
        Mei
       </i>
       . During 1583–88
       <a href="/wiki/Italians" title="Italians">
        Italian
       </a>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jesuits" title="Jesuits">
        Jesuits
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Michele_Ruggieri" title="Michele Ruggieri">
        Michele Ruggieri
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Matteo_Ricci" title="Matteo Ricci">
        Matteo Ricci
       </a>
       created a Portuguese–Chinese dictionary—the first ever European–Chinese dictionary.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-camus_101-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-camus-101">
         [101]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ricciDict_102-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-ricciDict-102">
         [102]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       For instance, as
       <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Empire" title="Portuguese Empire">
        Portuguese merchants
       </a>
       were presumably the first to introduce the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sweet_orange" title="Sweet orange">
        sweet orange
       </a>
       in Europe, in several modern
       <a href="/wiki/Indo-European_languages" title="Indo-European languages">
        Indo-European languages
       </a>
       the fruit has been named after them. Some examples are Albanian
       <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/portokall#Albanian" title="wikt:portokall">
        portokall
       </a>
       , Bulgarian
       <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/%D0%BF%D0%BE%D1%80%D1%82%D0%BE%D0%BA%D0%B0%D0%BB#Bulgarian" title="wikt:портокал">
        портокал
       </a>
       (
       <i>
        portokal
       </i>
       ), Greek
       <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/%CF%80%CE%BF%CF%81%CF%84%CE%BF%CE%BA%CE%AC%CE%BB%CE%B9#Greek" title="wikt:πορτοκάλι">
        πορτοκάλι
       </a>
       (
       <i>
        portokali
       </i>
       ),
       <a href="/wiki/Macedonian_language" title="Macedonian language">
        Macedonian
       </a>
       <i>
        portokal
       </i>
       , Persian
       <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/%D9%BE%D8%B1%D8%AA%D9%82%D8%A7%D9%84#Persian" title="wikt:پرتقال">
        پرتقال
       </a>
       (
       <i>
        porteghal
       </i>
       ), and Romanian
       <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/portocal%C4%83#Romanian" title="wikt:portocală">
        portocală
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-plantname_103-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-plantname-103">
         [103]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-OstergrenBosse2011_104-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-OstergrenBosse2011-104">
         [104]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Related names can be found in other languages, such as Arabic
       <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/%D8%A7%D9%84%D8%A8%D8%B1%D8%AA%D9%82%D8%A7%D9%84#Arabic" title="wikt:البرتقال">
        البرتقال
       </a>
       (
       <i>
        bourtouqal
       </i>
       ),
       <a href="/wiki/Georgian_language" title="Georgian language">
        Georgian
       </a>
       <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/%E1%83%A4%E1%83%9D%E1%83%A0%E1%83%97%E1%83%9D%E1%83%AE%E1%83%90%E1%83%9A%E1%83%98#Georgian" title="wikt:ფორთოხალი">
        ფორთოხალი
       </a>
       (
       <i>
        p'ort'oxali
       </i>
       ), Turkish
       <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/portakal#Turkish" title="wikt:portakal">
        portakal
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Amharic" title="Amharic">
        Amharic
       </a>
       <i>
        birtukan
       </i>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-plantname_103-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-plantname-103">
         [103]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Also, in
       <a href="/wiki/Regional_Italian" title="Regional Italian">
        southern Italian dialects
       </a>
       (e.g.
       <a href="/wiki/Neapolitan_language" title="Neapolitan language">
        Neapolitan
       </a>
       ), an orange is
       <i>
        <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/portogallo" title="wikt:portogallo">
         portogallo
        </a>
       </i>
       or
       <i>
        <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/it:purtuallo" title="wikt:it:purtuallo">
         purtuallo
        </a>
       </i>
       , literally "(the) Portuguese (one)", in contrast to
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Standard_Italian" title="Standard Italian">
        standard Italian
       </a>
       <i>
        arancia
       </i>
       .
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Derived_languages">
        Derived languages
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Portuguese_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Derived languages">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Portuguese-based_creole_languages" title="Portuguese-based creole languages">
        Portuguese-based creole languages
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:2014_Lusophony_Games_map.svg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2234" data-file-width="4500" height="109" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/2014_Lusophony_Games_map.svg/220px-2014_Lusophony_Games_map.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/2014_Lusophony_Games_map.svg/330px-2014_Lusophony_Games_map.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/2014_Lusophony_Games_map.svg/440px-2014_Lusophony_Games_map.svg.png 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:2014_Lusophony_Games_map.svg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Participating countries of the
         <a href="/wiki/Lusophony_Games" title="Lusophony Games">
          Lusophony Games
         </a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       Beginning in the 16th century, the extensive contacts between Portuguese travelers and settlers, African and Asian slaves, and local populations led to the appearance of many
       <a href="/wiki/Pidgin" title="Pidgin">
        pidgins
       </a>
       with varying amounts of Portuguese influence. As each of these pidgins became the mother tongue of succeeding generations, they evolved into fully fledged
       <a href="/wiki/Creole_language" title="Creole language">
        creole languages
       </a>
       , which remained in use in many parts of Asia, Africa and South America until the 18th century. Some Portuguese-based or Portuguese-influenced creoles are still spoken today, by over 3 million people worldwide, especially people of partial
       <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_people" title="Portuguese people">
        Portuguese
       </a>
       ancestry.
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Phonology">
        Phonology
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Portuguese_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Phonology">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_phonology" title="Portuguese phonology">
        Portuguese phonology
       </a>
      </div>
