      <table class="metadata mbox-small noprint selfref" role="presentation" style="background-color:#f9f9f9;border:1px solid #aaa;color:#000;width: 22em;">
       <tr>
        <td class="mbox-image">
         <a href="/wiki/International_Phonetic_Alphabet" title="International Phonetic Alphabet">
          <img alt="[]" data-file-height="100" data-file-width="75" height="40" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Parentesi_Quadre.svg/30px-Parentesi_Quadre.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Parentesi_Quadre.svg/45px-Parentesi_Quadre.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Parentesi_Quadre.svg/60px-Parentesi_Quadre.svg.png 2x" width="30"/>
         </a>
        </td>
        <td class="mbox-text plainlist" style="vertical-align:middle; font-size:95%;">
         <b>
          This article contains
          <a href="/wiki/International_Phonetic_Alphabet" title="International Phonetic Alphabet">
           IPA
          </a>
          phonetic symbols.
         </b>
         Without proper
         <a href="/wiki/International_Phonetic_Alphabet#Fonts" title="International Phonetic Alphabet">
          rendering support
         </a>
         , you may see
         <a href="/wiki/Specials_(Unicode_block)#Replacement_character" title="Specials (Unicode block)">
          question marks, boxes, or other symbols
         </a>
         instead of
         <a href="/wiki/Unicode" title="Unicode">
          Unicode
         </a>
         characters. For an introductory guide on IPA symbols, see
         <a href="/wiki/Help:IPA" title="Help:IPA">
          Help:IPA
         </a>
         .
        </td>
       </tr>
      </table>
      <p>
       Portuguese phonology is similar to those of languages such as
       <a href="/wiki/French_phonology" title="French phonology">
        French
       </a>
       (especially
       <a href="/wiki/Quebec_French_phonology" title="Quebec French phonology">
        that of Quebec
       </a>
       ), the
       <a href="/wiki/Gallo-Italic_languages" title="Gallo-Italic languages">
        Gallo-Italic languages
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Occitan_phonology" title="Occitan phonology">
        Occitan
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Catalan_phonology" title="Catalan phonology">
        Catalan
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Franco-Proven%C3%A7al_language" title="Franco-Provençal language">
        Franco-Provençal
       </a>
       , unlike
       <a href="/wiki/Spanish_phonology" title="Spanish phonology">
        that of Spanish
       </a>
       , which is similar to those of
       <a href="/wiki/Sardinian_language" title="Sardinian language">
        Sardinian
       </a>
       and the
       <a href="/wiki/Neapolitan_language" title="Neapolitan language">
        Southern Italian dialects
       </a>
       . Some would describe the phonology of Portuguese as a blend of
       <a href="/wiki/Spanish_language" title="Spanish language">
        Spanish
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Gallo-Romance_languages" title="Gallo-Romance languages">
        Gallo-Romance
       </a>
       (e.g.
       <a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">
        French
       </a>
       ) and the
       <a href="/wiki/Gallo-Italic_languages" title="Gallo-Italic languages">
        languages of northern Italy
       </a>
       (especially
       <a href="/wiki/Genoese_dialect" title="Genoese dialect">
        Genoese
       </a>
       ), but with a deeper
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Celtic_language" title="Celtic language">
        Celtic
       </a>
       influence.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-105">
        <a href="#cite_note-105">
         [105]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       There is a maximum of 9 oral vowels, 2 semivowels and 21 consonants; though some varieties of the language have fewer phonemes. There are also five
       <a href="/wiki/Nasal_vowel" title="Nasal vowel">
        nasal vowels
       </a>
       , which some linguists regard as allophones of the oral vowels.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Vowels">
        Vowels
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Portuguese_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Vowels">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:European_Portuguese_vowel_chart.svg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="720" data-file-width="980" height="184" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/European_Portuguese_vowel_chart.svg/250px-European_Portuguese_vowel_chart.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/European_Portuguese_vowel_chart.svg/375px-European_Portuguese_vowel_chart.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/European_Portuguese_vowel_chart.svg/500px-European_Portuguese_vowel_chart.svg.png 2x" width="250"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:European_Portuguese_vowel_chart.svg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Chart of monophthongs of the Portuguese of Lisbon, with its
         <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
          /ɐ, ɐ̃/
         </span>
         in central
         <a href="/wiki/Schwa" title="Schwa">
          schwa
         </a>
         position.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Like
       <a href="/wiki/Catalan_language" title="Catalan language">
        Catalan
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/German_language" title="German language">
        German
       </a>
       , Portuguese uses vowel quality to contrast stressed syllables with unstressed syllables: isolated vowels tend to be
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Vowel_height" title="Vowel height">
        raised
       </a>
       , and in some cases centralized, when unstressed.
      </p>
      <h3>

         <small>
          <a href="/wiki/Lateral_consonant" title="Lateral consonant">
           lateral
          </a>
         </small>
        </th>
        <td>
        </td>
        <td>
         <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
          <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Alveolar_lateral_approximant" title="Alveolar lateral approximant">
           l
          </a>
         </span>
        </td>
        <td>
         <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
          <a href="/wiki/Palatal_lateral_approximant" title="Palatal lateral approximant">
           ʎ
          </a>
         </span>
        </td>
        <td>
        </td>
        <td>
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <th rowspan="2">
         <a href="/wiki/Rhotic_consonant" title="Rhotic consonant">
          Rhotic
         </a>
        </th>
        <th>
         <small>
          <a href="/wiki/Trill_consonant" title="Trill consonant">
           trill
          </a>
          /
          <a href="/wiki/Fricative_consonant" title="Fricative consonant">
           fricative
          </a>
         </small>
        </th>
        <td>
        </td>
        <td colspan="2">
         <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
          ʁ
         </span>
        </td>
        <td>
        </td>
        <td>
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <th>
         <small>
          <a href="/wiki/Flap_consonant" title="Flap consonant">
           flap
          </a>
         </small>
        </th>
        <td>
        </td>
        <td>
         <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
          <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Alveolar_flap" title="Alveolar flap">
           ɾ
          </a>
         </span>
        </td>
        <td>
        </td>
        <td>
        </td>
        <td>
        </td>
       </tr>
      </table>
      <p>
       <b>
        Phonetic notes
       </b>
      </p>
      <ul>
       <li>
        Semivowels contrast with unstressed high vowels in verbal conjugation, as in
        <i>
         (eu) rio
        </i>
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         /ˈʁi.u/
        </span>
        and
        <i>
         (ele) riu
        </i>
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         /ˈʁiw/
        </span>
        .
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-110">
         <a href="#cite_note-110">
          [110]
         </a>
        </sup>
        Phonologists discuss whether their nature is vowel or consonant.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-111">
         <a href="#cite_note-111">
          [111]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
       <li>
        In most of Brazil and Angola, the consonant hereafter denoted as
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         /ɲ/
        </span>
        is realized as a
        <a href="/wiki/Nasal_palatal_approximant" title="Nasal palatal approximant">
         nasal palatal approximant
        </a>
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         [
         <a href="/wiki/Nasal_palatal_approximant" title="Nasal palatal approximant">
          j̃
         </a>
         ]
        </span>
        , which
        <a href="/wiki/Nasalization" title="Nasalization">
         nasalizes
        </a>
        the vowel that precedes it:
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         [ˈnĩj̃u]
        </span>
        .
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-112">
         <a href="#cite_note-112">
          [112]
         </a>
        </sup>
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-113">
         <a href="#cite_note-113">
          [113]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="#CITEREFBisol2005">
         Bisol (2005
        </a>
        :122) proposes that Portuguese possesses labio-velar stops
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         /kʷ/
        </span>
        and
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         /ɡʷ/
        </span>
        as additional phonemes rather than sequences of a velar stop and
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         /w/
        </span>
        .
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-labialized_velar_-_Bisol_109-1">
         <a href="#cite_note-labialized_velar_-_Bisol-109">
          [109]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
       <li>
        The consonant hereafter denoted as
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         /ʁ/
        </span>
        has a variety of realizations depending on dialect. In Europe, it is typically a
        <a href="/wiki/Uvular_trill" title="Uvular trill">
         uvular trill
        </a>
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         [ʀ]
        </span>
        ; however, a pronunciation as a
        <a href="/wiki/Voiced_uvular_fricative" title="Voiced uvular fricative">
         voiced uvular fricative
        </a>
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         [ʁ]
        </span>
        may be becoming dominant in urban areas. There is also a realization as a
        <a href="/wiki/Voiceless_uvular_fricative" title="Voiceless uvular fricative">
         voiceless uvular fricative
        </a>
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         [χ]
        </span>
        , and the original pronunciation as an
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Alveolar_trill" title="Alveolar trill">
         alveolar trill
        </a>
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         [r]
        </span>
        also remains very common in various dialects.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-114">
         <a href="#cite_note-114">
          [114]
         </a>
        </sup>
        A common realization of the word-initial
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         /r/
        </span>
        in the Lisbon accent is a voiced uvular trill fricative
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         [
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Voiced_raised_uvular_trill" title="Voiced raised uvular trill">
          ʀ̝
         </a>
         ]
        </span>
        .
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gr157_115-0">
         <a href="#cite_note-gr157-115">
          [115]
         </a>
        </sup>
        In Brazil,
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         /ʁ/
        </span>
        can be
        <a href="/wiki/Velar_consonant" title="Velar consonant">
         velar
        </a>
        ,
        <a href="/wiki/Uvular_consonant" title="Uvular consonant">
         uvular
        </a>
        , or
        <a href="/wiki/Glottal_consonant" title="Glottal consonant">
         glottal
        </a>
        and may be voiceless unless between voiced sounds;
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-116">
         <a href="#cite_note-116">
          [116]
         </a>
        </sup>
        it is usually pronounced as a
        <a href="/wiki/Voiceless_velar_fricative" title="Voiceless velar fricative">
         voiceless velar fricative
        </a>
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         [x]
        </span>
        , a
        <a href="/wiki/Voiceless_glottal_fricative" title="Voiceless glottal fricative">
         voiceless glottal fricative
        </a>
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         [h]
        </span>
        or
        <a href="/wiki/Voiceless_uvular_fricative" title="Voiceless uvular fricative">
         voiceless uvular fricative
        </a>
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         [χ]
        </span>
        . See also
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Guttural_R#Portuguese" title="Guttural R">
          Guttural R in Portuguese
         </a>
        </i>
        .
       </li>
       <li>
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         /s/
        </span>
        and
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         /z/
        </span>
        are normally
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lamino-alveolar_consonant" title="Lamino-alveolar consonant">
         lamino-alveolar
        </a>
        , as in English. However, a number of dialects in northern Portugal pronounce
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         /s/
        </span>
        and
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         /z/
        </span>
        as
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Apico-alveolar" title="Apico-alveolar">
         apico-alveolar
        </a>
        <a href="/wiki/Sibilant" title="Sibilant">
         sibilants
        </a>
        (sounding somewhat like a soft
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         [ʃ]
        </span>
        or
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         [ʒ]
        </span>
        ), as in the Romance languages of northern Iberia. A very few northeastern Portugal dialects still maintain the medieval distinction between apical and laminal sibilants (written
        <i>
         s/ss
        </i>
        and
        <i>
         c/ç/z
        </i>
        , respectively).
       </li>
       <li>
        As a phoneme,
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         /tʃ/
        </span>
        only occurs in loanwords, with a tendency for speakers to substitute in
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         /ʃ/
        </span>
        . However,
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         [tʃ]
        </span>
        is an
        <a href="/wiki/Allophone" title="Allophone">
         allophone
        </a>
        of
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         /t/
        </span>
        before
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         /i/
        </span>
        in a number of Brazilian dialects. Similarly,
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         [dʒ]
        </span>
        is an allophone of
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         /d/
        </span>
        in the same contexts.
       </li>
       <li>
        In northern and central Portugal, the voiced stops
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         /b/
        </span>
        ,
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         /d/
        </span>
        ,
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         /ɡ/
        </span>
        are usually lenited to
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fricative" title="Fricative">
         fricatives
        </a>
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         [β]
        </span>
        ,
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         [ð]
        </span>
        , and
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         [ɣ]
        </span>
        respectively, except at the beginning of words, or after nasal vowels;
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-117">
         <a href="#cite_note-117">
          [117]
         </a>
        </sup>
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-118">
         <a href="#cite_note-118">
          [118]
         </a>
        </sup>
        a
        <a href="/wiki/Spanish_phonology#Phonetic_notes" title="Spanish phonology">
         similar process
        </a>
        occurs in Spanish.
       </li>
      </ul>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Grammar">
        Grammar
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Portuguese_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Grammar">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_grammar" title="Portuguese grammar">
        Portuguese grammar
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       A notable aspect of the grammar of Portuguese is the verb. Morphologically, more verbal inflections from classical Latin have been preserved by Portuguese than by any other major
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Romance_language" title="Romance language">
        Romance language
       </a>
       . The Portuguese and Spanish grammars are very close. It also has some innovations not found in other Romance languages (except Galician and the Fala):
      </p>
      <ul>
       <li>
        The
        <a href="/wiki/Present_perfect" title="Present perfect">
         present perfect
        </a>
        has an iterative sense unique to the Galician-Portuguese language group. It denotes an action or a series of actions that began in the past and are expected to keep repeating in the future. For instance, the sentence
        <i>
         Tenho tentado falar com ela
        </i>
        would be translated to "I have been trying to talk to her", not "I have tried to talk to her". On the other hand, the correct translation of the question "Have you heard the latest news?" is not
        <i>
         *Tem ouvido a última notícia?
        </i>
        , but
        <i>
         Ouviu a última notícia?
        </i>
        , since no repetition is implied.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-119">
         <a href="#cite_note-119">
          [119]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Vernacular" title="Vernacular">
         Vernacular
        </a>
        Portuguese still uses the future
        <a href="/wiki/Subjunctive_mood" title="Subjunctive mood">
         subjunctive mood
        </a>
        , which developed from medieval
        <a href="/wiki/West_Iberian_languages" title="West Iberian languages">
         West Iberian Romance
        </a>
        and in present-day Spanish and Galician has almost entirely fallen into disuse. The future subjunctive appears in dependent clauses that denote a condition that must be fulfilled in the future so that the independent clause will occur. English normally employs the present tense under the same circumstances:
       </li>
      </ul>
      <dl>
       <dd>
        <i>
         Se eu
        </i>
        for
        <i>
         eleito presidente, mudarei a lei.
        </i>
       </dd>
       <dd>
        If
        <i>
         I should be
        </i>
        elected president, I will change the law.
       </dd>
      </dl>
      <dl>
       <dd>
        <i>
         Quando
        </i>
        fores
        <i>
         mais velho, vais entender.
        </i>
       </dd>
       <dd>
        When
        <i>
         you grow
        </i>
        older, you will understand.
       </dd>
      </dl>
      <ul>
       <li>
        The personal
        <a href="/wiki/Infinitive" title="Infinitive">
         infinitive
        </a>
        : infinitives can
        <a href="/wiki/Inflection" title="Inflection">
         inflect
        </a>
        according to their subject in
        <a href="/wiki/Grammatical_person" title="Grammatical person">
         person
        </a>
        and
        <a href="/wiki/Grammatical_number" title="Grammatical number">
         number
        </a>
        , often showing who is expected to perform a certain action; cf.
        <i>
         É melhor voltares
        </i>
        "It is better [for you] to go back",
        <i>
         É melhor voltarmos
        </i>
        "It is better [for us] to go back." Perhaps for this reason, infinitive clauses replace subjunctive clauses more often in Portuguese than in other Romance languages.
       </li>
      </ul>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Writing_system">
        Writing system
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Portuguese_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Writing system">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <table cellpadding="4" cellspacing="0" class="infobox bordered" style="width:250px; font-size:95%; float:right; float:right;">
       <caption>
        <big>
         <b>
          Written varieties
         </b>
        </big>
       </caption>
       <tr>
        <th style="background:#ddd;">
         Portugal and non-1990 Agreement countries
        </th>
        <th style="background:#ddd;">
         Brazil and 1990 Agreement countries
        </th>
        <th style="background:#ddd;">
         translation
        </th>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td>
         dire
         <b>
          c
         </b>
         ção
        </td>
        <td>
         direção
        </td>
        <td>
         direction
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td>
         ó
         <b>
          p
         </b>
         timo
        </td>
        <td>
         ótimo
        </td>
        <td>
         best, excellent, optimal
        </td>
       </tr>
      </table>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_orthography" title="Portuguese orthography">
        Portuguese orthography
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       Portuguese is written with 26 letters of the
       <a href="/wiki/Latin_script" title="Latin script">
        Latin script
       </a>
       , making use of five
       <a href="/wiki/Diacritic" title="Diacritic">
        diacritics
       </a>
       to denote stress, vowel height, contraction, nasalization, and etymological
       <a href="/wiki/Assibilation" title="Assibilation">
        assibilation
       </a>
       (
       <a href="/wiki/Acute_accent" title="Acute accent">
        acute accent
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Circumflex" title="Circumflex">
        circumflex
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Grave_accent" title="Grave accent">
        grave accent
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Tilde" title="Tilde">
        tilde
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Cedilla" title="Cedilla">
        cedilla
       </a>
       ). The
       <a href="/wiki/Diaeresis_(diacritic)" title="Diaeresis (diacritic)">
        trema
       </a>
       was also formerly used in Brazilian Portuguese, and can still be encountered in words derived from proper names in other languages, such as Anhangüera and mülleriano.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-120">
        <a href="#cite_note-120">
         [120]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-121">
        <a href="#cite_note-121">
         [121]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Accented characters and
       <a href="/wiki/Digraph_(orthography)" title="Digraph (orthography)">
        digraphs
       </a>
       are not counted as separate letters for
       <a href="/wiki/Collation" title="Collation">
        collation
       </a>
       purposes.
      </p>

      <div aria-label="Portals" class="noprint metadata navbox" role="navigation" style="font-weight:bold;padding:0.4em 2em">
       <ul style="margin:0.1em 0 0">
        <li style="display:inline">
         <span style="display:inline-block;white-space:nowrap">

          <span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=The+Europeans%2C+Second+Edition%3A+A+Geography+of+People%2C+Culture%2C+and+Environment&amp;rft.pages=129&amp;rft.pub=Guilford+Press&amp;rft.date=2011&amp;rft.isbn=978-1-60918-140-6&amp;rft.au=Ostergren%2C+Robert+C.&amp;rft.au=Le+Bosse%2C+Mathias&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fbooks.google.com%2Fbooks%3Fid%3Dy-1fwix23zMC%26pg%3DPA129&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3APortuguese+language">
           <span style="display:none;">

        <li id="cite_note-105">
         <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
          <b>
           <a href="#cite_ref-105">
            ^
           </a>
          </b>
         </span>
         <span class="reference-text">

        <li id="cite_note-ReferenceA-106">
         <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
          <b>
           <a href="#cite_ref-ReferenceA_106-0">
            ^
           </a>
          </b>
         </span>
         <span class="reference-text">
          <a href="#CITEREFCruz-Ferreira1995">
           Cruz-Ferreira (1995
          </a>
          :91)
         </span>
        </li>
        <li id="cite_note-107">
         <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
          <b>
           <a href="#cite_ref-107">
            ^
           </a>
          </b>
         </span>
         <span class="reference-text">
          <a href="#CITEREFBarbosaAlbano2004">
           Barbosa &amp; Albano (2004
          </a>
          :228–229)
         </span>
        </li>
        <li id="cite_note-labialized_velar_-_Carvalho-108">
         <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
          <b>
           <a href="#cite_ref-labialized_velar_-_Carvalho_108-0">
            ^
           </a>
          </b>
         </span>
         <span class="reference-text">
          <a class="external text" href="http://cl.up.pt/elingup/vol4n1/article/article_2.pdf" rel="nofollow">
           Sobre os Ditongos do Português Europeu
          </a>
          . Carvalho, Joana. Faculdade de Letras da Universidade do Porto. Page 20 (page 10 of PDF file).
          <b>
           Citation:
          </b>
          <i>
           A conclusão será que nos encontramos em presença de dois segmentos fonológicos /kʷ/ e /ɡʷ/, respetivamente, com uma articulação vocálica. Bisol (2005:122), tal como Freitas (1997), afirma que não estamos em presença de um ataque ramificado. Neste caso, a glide, juntamente com a vogal que a sucede, forma um ditongo no nível pós-lexical.
          </i>
          Esta conclusão implica um aumento do número de segmentos no inventário segmental fonológico do português.
         </span>
        </li>
        <li id="cite_note-labialized_velar_-_Bisol-109">
         <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
          ^
          <a href="#cite_ref-labialized_velar_-_Bisol_109-0">
           <sup>
            <i>
             <b>
              a
             </b>
            </i>
           </sup>
          </a>
          <a href="#cite_ref-labialized_velar_-_Bisol_109-1">
           <sup>
            <i>
             <b>
              b
             </b>
            </i>
           </sup>
          </a>
         </span>
         <span class="reference-text">
          <a href="#CITEREFBisol2005">
           Bisol (2005
          </a>
          :122).
          <b>
           Citation:
          </b>
          <i>
           A proposta é que a sequencia consoante velar + glide posterior seja indicada no léxico como uma unidade monofonemática /kʷ/ e /ɡʷ/. O glide que, nete caso, situa-se no ataque não-ramificado, forma com a vogal seguinte um ditongo crescente em nível pós lexical. Ditongos crescentes somente se formam neste nível. Em resumo, a consoante velar e o glide posterior, quando seguidos de a/o, formam uma só unidade fonológica, ou seja, um segmento consonantal com articulação secundária vocálica, em outros termos, um segmento complexo.
          </i>
         </span>
        </li>
        <li id="cite_note-110">
         <span class="mw-cite-backlink">

           <a href="#cite_ref-110">
            ^
           </a>
          </b>
         </span>
         <span class="reference-text">
          <a href="#CITEREFRodrigues2012">
           Rodrigues (2012
          </a>
          :39–40)
         </span>
        </li>

          <span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Modern+Portuguese+%28A+Reference+Grammar%29&amp;rft.place=New+Haven&amp;rft.pub=Yale+University+Press&amp;rft.date=2002&amp;rft.isbn=978-0-300-09155-7&amp;rft.aulast=Perini&amp;rft.aufirst=M%C3%A1rio+Alberto&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3APortuguese+language">

        <li id="cite_note-114">
         <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
          <b>
           <a href="#cite_ref-114">
            ^

         Vossa Mercê
        </i>
        to
        <i>
         Você
        </i>
        , Portuguese Studies Review 3.2, Durham: University of New Hampshire, 1995
       </li>
       <li>
        Lindley Cintra, Luís F.
        <a class="external text" href="http://cvc.instituto-camoes.pt/hlp/biblioteca/novaproposta.pdf" rel="nofollow">
         <i>
          Nova Proposta de Classificação dos Dialectos Galego- Portugueses
         </i>
        </a>
        (PDF) Boletim de Filologia, Lisboa, Centro de Estudos Filológicos, 1971.
       </li>
      </ul>

                   </b>
                   indicates

                   </a>
                  </li>

                   <a href="/wiki/Variety_(linguistics)" title="Variety (linguistics)">
